--- Commit Message ---
LU-17427 mdt: reduce hold time for BFL rename lock

In non-parallel rename, the order of resource locking follows
a fixed order: first global BFL, then (up to) 4 FID locks.
This means the BFL can be held for a long time if any client
holding one of the FID locks is non-responsive for some reason.
Especially in a big cluster where hundreds or thousands clients
exist doing various workloads.

To reduce hold time for BFL lock, we restructure the locking
into two phases,
1. get the 4 child locks first (to cancel the majority of
lock holders)
2. try to get the BFL resource lock if it is uncontended
3a. if BFL is contended then drop child locks and wait for it
3b. re-get the child locks if they were dropped in 3a

Note in phase 1 there's no BFL umbrella anymore, which in turn
may introduce deadlock, hence some order logic is added, e.g.
mdt_rename_determine_lock_order() order by fid if objs belong
to different parents.

> perf results:
1. two active clients with only renames:
max_dirs     without-patch        with
500x500         14418             14276
150x150         20419             20210

2. slow clients scenario, QPS=10 and 5s pause where P(X)=1%
for master and P(X)=0.1% for patch (not quite sure if the P is
reasonable or not),
Metric (ms/req)	  without-patch	  with
Average Latency	  205.76	  21.50

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2025-02-14 04:16:04.000000000) ---

--- Message (kg.xu, 2025-02-21 08:44:24.000000000) ---
Patch Set 15:

> Patch Set 15:
> 
> With only 2 mountpoints there is serialization on the client VFS rename lock, so running multiple threads may not show the proper scaling. If you could run the rename test within multiple mountpoints on the two clients to avoid contention on the VFS lock?

Back. This time the mount points increases to 6 and we focused on directory-only-renames() for the sake of BFL.

Env:
- 1 client, 1 host (bare-metal + ESSD), 2 MDS, 6 mount points, 96 threads in total.
- Duration: 30 seconds.
- Variable: max_dirs – For the operation rename(pdir1/dir1, pdir2/dir2), all pdirs and dirs are randomly selected from [0, max_dirs). A larger max_dirs reduces the likelihood of collisions.

Results:
max_dirs     without-patch        with
500                 14418                 14276 
150                 20419                 20210

The results show that the performance difference between the patched and unpatched versions is minimal, with a difference of less than or close to 1%.




Besides, I make another dir-only-rename-test to simulate a slow client scenario: when BFL is acquired, there is a probability P(X) of encountering a slow child lock holder. I made up 2 numbers as following,
- Master branch: P(X) = 1%
- Patched version: P(X) = 0.1%

Here 
1. cancel the majority of lock holders, drop those locks, then 
2. get the BFL resource lock and 
3. re-lock the children, 
there should be a relatively short window between 2->3, chance to meet a slow client should be much lower.

Env:
- 1 client, 1 host, 2 MDS, 2 mount points, 2 threads.
- Query rate: 10 QPS.
- Event: If a slow client is encountered, wait for 5 seconds.

Results:
Metric (ms/req)	  Without Patch	With Patch
Average Latency	  205.76	                21.50

The patch version as expected works better than the master version, reducing the average request time from 205.76 ms to 21.50 ms.

You may use mdt_object_lock_try() for BFL lock, if it fails to lock BFL, then drop locks taken and restart from beginning, otherwise you can just continue.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2025-03-04 13:20:41.000000000) ---
Patch Set 24:

> You may use mdt_object_lock_try() for BFL lock, if it fails to lock
 > BFL, then drop locks taken and restart from beginning, otherwise
 > you can just continue.

Even better!  That avoids overhead in the common case of an uncontended lock, and only retries the locking if needed.  It might be possible to optimize this based on recent locking history, with a decaying average of whether the BFL was contended or not?

--- Message (kg.xu, 2025-03-05 09:04:48.000000000) ---
Patch Set 24:

> Patch Set 24:
> 
> > You may use mdt_object_lock_try() for BFL lock, if it fails to lock
>  > BFL, then drop locks taken and restart from beginning, otherwise
>  > you can just continue.
> 
> Even better!  That avoids overhead in the common case of an uncontended lock, and only retries the locking if needed.  It might be possible to optimize this based on recent locking history, with a decaying average of whether the BFL was contended or not?

Indeed, it's feasible to separate the processing logic `mdt_object_lock[_try]` based on the lock contention intensity, which could be reasoned about given BFL-locking history through sliding window or decaying.

Here, how about we implement above improvement into another patch, and finish current patch as the first step?

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2025-03-05 09:32:13.000000000) ---
Patch Set 24:

Yes, definitely you start with the simple mechanism of just using trylock before dropping the FID locks and retrying.  It might be useful to measure how much time is spent calling trylock in the failure case, to see if it is even worthwhile to optimize.

Then, if there is still a significant performance improvement to be had and you have time/interest, trying a second patch that keeps a history of recent success/failure of trylock to try and optimize away that overhead.

--- Message (kg.xu, 2025-03-06 03:49:18.000000000) ---
Patch Set 24:

thanks！

--- Message (Lai Siyao, 2025-03-06 04:43:16.000000000) ---
Patch Set 24:

> Patch Set 24:
> 
> > Patch Set 24:
> > 
> > You may use mdt_object_lock_try() for BFL lock, if it fails to lock BFL, then drop locks taken and restart from beginning, otherwise you can just continue.
> 
> Trying, with some technical questions that I’d appreciate your help with:
> - As mdt_object_lock_try() called mdt_object_lock_internal(cache=false), what might be the effect here, compared with (cache=true)? Particularly in this lock fail then retry context;

> 
> thanks！

Normally MDTs don't cache locks taken, so it's the same as mdt_object_lock(),

root_obj is used to locate the MDT0, where BFL lock will be sent to.

> ldlm.namespaces.mdt-lustre-MDT0000_UUID.lock_count=17074

It only appears if (rename_lock_try.enabled && MDSCOUNT >= 2). P.S. at least from my sampled results.

Maybe my usage of try-lock is inappropriate?


static int mdt_rename_lock(struct mdt_thread_info *info,
			   struct mdt_lock_handle *lh, bool trylock)
{
        ...

	mdt_lock_reg_init(lh, LCK_EX);
	ibits = trylock ? 0 : MDS_INODELOCK_UPDATE;
	trybits = trylock ? MDS_INODELOCK_UPDATE : 0;
	rc = mdt_object_lock_internal(info, obj, &LUSTRE_BFL_FID, lh,
				      &ibits, trybits, false);
	if (trylock && (ibits & MDS_INODELOCK_UPDATE))
		RETURN(0);
	RETURN(rc);
}

Follow up, issue seems from LDLM,

ldlm_handle_enqueue()
    err = ldlm_lock_enqueue(env, ns, &lock, cookie, &flags);
    if (err) {
	if ((int)err < 0)
		rc = (int)err;
	GOTO(out, err);
    }
out:
    if (lock != NULL)
        if (rc != 0 && !(flags & LDLM_FL_RESENT))
            ldlm_lock_cancel(lock);   
}

if err=ELDLM_LOCK_ABORTED(301>0, happens when try lock failed), seems lock cancel would not be called. I add corresponding err logic the resource leak disappeared. Correct me if any mistakes. Thanks a lot.
